          </li>
          <li class="cat-item cat-item-36">

         <div class="entry">
          <article class="post clearfix">
           <div class="post-inner-wrapper">
            <header class="post-header clearfix">
             <div class="author_avatar">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/bd5f9ee14f8d6b023f49f128264eebf0?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2F1.gravatar.com%2Favatar%2Fad516503a11cd5ca435acc9bb6523536%3Fs%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
             </div>
             <div class="post-date">
              <p>
               <strong>
                Jun
               </strong>
               <span>
                13
               </span>
               2011
              </p>
             </div>
             <h1 class="post-title">
              <a href="http://thepioneerwoman.com/cooking/2011/06/perfect-iced-coffee/" title="Perfect Iced Coffee">
               Perfect Iced Coffee
              </a>
             </h1>
             <div class="meta-tasks">
              <span class="author">
               Posted by Ree
              </span>
              <a class="comment-number-wrap" href="http://thepioneerwoman.com/cooking/2011/06/perfect-iced-coffee/#comments">
               <div class="comment-number">
                1252
               </div>
               <span>
                Comments
               </span>
              </a>
              <a class="print-icon" href="#recipe-form-144285" id="print-recipe-link-144285">
               Print Recipe
              </a>
             </div>
            </header>
            <div class="post-padding">
             <p>
              <a href="http://thepioneerwoman.com/cooking/wp-content/uploads/sites/3/2011/06/iced.jpg">
               <img alt="iced" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-13879 frame-img width_426" height="640" src="http://thepioneerwoman.com/cooking/wp-content/uploads/sites/3/2011/06/iced.jpg" width="426"/>
              </a>
              Iced coffee is my life. When I wake up, often around the time party animals on the west coast are just heading home, I start each day not with a cup of freshly brewed hot java, but with a tall, blessed glass of creamy iced coffee in a glass. Ive been an iced coffee freakazoid for years and years. To say I couldnt live without it is an understatement. It gives me the tools I need to cope.
             </p>
             <p>
              Iced coffee is a complicated thing, and there are many different approaches. One would think that one could merely pour brewed coffee into a glass full of ice and call it a daybut I find that method extremely flawed. First, no matter how packed with ice the glass is, once the hot coffee hits, some of the ice is bound to melt. This has two disastrous results:
             </p>
             <p>
              1. The overall strength of the coffee flavor is diluted.
              <br/>
              2. The iced coffee isnt as cold as it could (or should) be. The finished glass of iced coffee should be frigid, not sorta cold with half-melted ice cubes floating around.
             </p>
             <p>
              Given the previous set of facts, one would assume that the logical solution would be to brew hot coffee, then transfer the brew to the fridge, allow it to cool, and use it to make iced coffee from there. Its an okay solution, one I subscribed to for quite awhileuntil I picked up an issue of Imbibe Magazine three summers ago. It contained a
              <a href="http://www.imbibemagazine.com/Iced-Coffee-How-To" target="_blank">
               huge spread
              </a>
              on the subject of iced coffee, and suggested the following cold-brew method for creating a sort of iced coffee concentrate. I tried it immediately, have made it this way ever since, and can tell you that there is no better (or simpler) method for having the most delicious iced coffee at your fingertips.
             </p>
             <p>
              There are reasons this method results in a smoother, richer, more delicious concentrate than simply brewing strong coffee and refrigerating it. I would take the time to explain them to you if I knew what they were. But since I dont, Im just going to show you instead.
             </p>
             <p>
              (Note: Ive totally adapted/tweaked coffee/water amounts to suit my own tastes. Experiment to find your own perfect ratio.)
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825898241/" title="REE_4983 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_4983" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5280/5825898241_789098be9c_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              I start with a big ol container. I love these food storage containers, by the way. I got these at restaurant supply, but Sams Club had them last time I was there.
             </p>
             <p>
              You can use a big bowl, a large pitchereven a really clean bucket will work if youre going for a huge quantity. (Or you can halve the original quantity and use a pitcher.)
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826453502/" title="REE_4984 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_4984" class="width_426 frame-img" height="640" src="http://farm2.static.flickr.com/1423/5826453502_b2b2d0c22c_z.jpg" width="426"/>
              </a>
              Rip open a pound of ground coffee. Any kind will do; the stronger and richer the better.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825898923/" title="REE_4986 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_4986" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3192/5825898923_84529146b3_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Pour in the coffee.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826454162/" title="REE_4991 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_4991" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5200/5826454162_b8b439098f_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Mount Bliss. Who invented coffee, anyway? They should be awarded the keys to the city.
             </p>
             <p>
              Or, at the very least, my heart.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826454394/" title="REE_4995 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_4995" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2347/5826454394_a19ae5941f_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Pour in 8 quarts (2 gallons) cold water.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825899927/" title="REE_4998 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_4998" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5061/5825899927_a68178d1a8_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Give it a stir to make sure all the grounds make contact with the water
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825900163/" title="REE_5000 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5000" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5109/5825900163_47e0554a9d_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Then cover the container and go live your life as the coffee steeps for at least eight hours. (And you can go much longer if youd like.)
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826455142/" title="REE_5001 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5001" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3344/5826455142_6671df733f_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              When the time has passed, grab a separate container and place a fine mesh strainer over the top.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825900725/" title="REE_5008 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5008" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3170/5825900725_bcdbcc6ff0_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Place a couple of layers of cheesecloth inside the strainer
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825901015/" title="REE_5010 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5010" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3198/5825901015_413bdda8d8_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              And slowly pour the steeped coffee through the strainer.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826456300/" title="REE_5015 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5015" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3195/5826456300_dd6645eda9_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Itll take awhile for all the liquid to pass through. (Doesnt this look like one of the acid pools at Yellowstone?)
             </p>
             <p>
              My friend
              <a href="http://www.anotherchanceranch.com/" target="_blank">
               Julie
              </a>
              is there right now.
             </p>
             <p>
              Hi, Julie!
             </p>
             <p>
              Oh. Guess she didnt hear me.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825901943/" title="REE_5019 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5019" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2785/5825901943_e615390064_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Use a spoon to gently press/force the last of the liquid through. And note: Ive tried the straining method without the cheesecloth, and stray grounds did make it through the mesh strainer. Definitely try to use cheesecloth (or even paper towels) to filter out the finer pieces.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826457014/" title="REE_5022 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5022" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5152/5826457014_235a0aab5d_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              And there we have it. The dregs (left)and the gold (right.)
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825902703/" title="REE_5028 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5028" class="width_426 frame-img" height="640" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5232/5825902703_3b2662f4a5_z.jpg" width="426"/>
              </a>
              You can store the liquid in the same container, or you can transfer it to a pitcher or other dispenser. Though its difficult to wait, I refrigerate this gorgeous concoction before consuming it. Its meant to be cold!
             </p>
             <p>
              Note: this amount of coffee concentrate lasts me a good three weeks to a month if kept tightly covered in the fridge.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825903123/" title="REE_5033 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5033" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3113/5825903123_400c5e46a5_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Now, when youre ready to make yourself an iced coffee, you can do two things. Start by filling a glass with ice.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826458140/" title="REE_5037 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5037" class="width_426 frame-img" height="640" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5238/5826458140_48b1f23aef_z.jpg" width="426"/>
              </a>
              Reach into the fridge and dispense enough of the coffee liquid to fill the glass half full (or maybe a little more).
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826458338/" title="REE_5039 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5039" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2716/5826458338_583de58da9_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Splash in skim, 2%, or whole milkor, if youre a naughty, naughty bad girl like me: half-and-half.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826458530/" title="REE_5040 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5040" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5223/5826458530_6e69ea4533_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Make that naughty, naughty, naughty, bad, bad girl.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825903919/" title="REE_5042 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5042" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2133/5825903919_62d279981d_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Add enough sugar to achieve the level of sweetness you like, or you can drizzle in vanilla or hazelnut syrup if you have those kinds of things lying around.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825904305/" title="REE_5047 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5047" class="width_426 frame-img" height="640" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3494/5825904305_46ee440570_z.jpg" width="426"/>
              </a>
              Stir it all up
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825904587/" title="REE_5050 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5050" class="width_426 frame-img" height="640" src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2563/5825904587_e14136ab78_z.jpg" width="426"/>
              </a>
              Stick in a straw
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825905359/" title="REE_5055 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5055" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3046/5825905359_60345cf09f_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              And go fer it. Look at that miracle. The ice is all there. The flavors all there.
             </p>
             <p>
              Im all there.
             </p>
             <h6>
              VARIATION: VIETNAMESE ICED COFFEE
             </h6>
             <p>
              And now for something entirely different. Samebut different.
             </p>
             <p>
              This is a variation on classic Vietnamese Iced Coffee (also recommended by Imbibe), which actually does begin with a hot brewbut Im using the cold stuff.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826461224/" title="REE_5062 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5062" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3040/5826461224_580d890ee7_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Fill the glass with ice and coffee concentrate as we did before, then crack open a can of sweetened condensed milk.
             </p>
             <p>
              A glorious substance. One you should get to know better if you dont already.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825906637/" title="REE_5066 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5066" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2422/5825906637_55bb77f42b_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Drizzle in at least 2 tablespoons for a big glass (I wound up adding three.)
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5825906889/" title="REE_5069 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5069" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5277/5825906889_053e95496b_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              CometoMAMA.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826461970/" title="REE_5071 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5071" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3342/5826461970_d0eb8178f0_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              On top of this, add a small splash of milk or half-and-half.
             </p>
             <p>
              (I recommend the latter, of course.)
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826462162/" title="REE_5073 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5073" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2702/5826462162_595528b1f6_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Glorious.
             </p>
             <p>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/pioneerwoman/5826462676/" title="REE_5075 by Ree Drummond / The Pioneer Woman, on Flickr">
               <img alt="REE_5075" class="width_630 frame-img" height="419" src="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3358/5826462676_2bb2c74280_z.jpg" width="630"/>
              </a>
              Stir, take a small sip, and add a little more sweetened condensed milk if needed.
             </p>
             <p>
              Ive tried all combinations of milk, half-and-half, sugar, artificial sweeteners, flavored syrups, and sweetened condensed milk, and I will tell you that there is no more winning combo than the half-and-half/sweetened condensed milk mixture. It is out-of-this-world creamy and wonderful, and is worth at least a spot in your weekend rotation if youre not willing to go there daily.
             </p>
             <p>
              Either way, try this cold-brewed method of iced coffee sometime soon. The flavor, convenience (and cost savings) can not be underestimated.
             </p>
             <p>
              Love,
              <br/>
              Pioneer Woman
             </p>
             <p>
              Heres a link to the printable recipe:
             </p>

              <h4 class="recipe-sub-head">
               Ingredients
              </h4>
              <ul>
               <li>
                <span itemprop="ingredient" itemscope="" itemtype="http://data-vocabulary.org/RecipeIngredient">
                 <span itemprop="amount">
                  1 pound
                 </span>
                 <span itemprop="name">
                  Ground Coffee (good, Rich Roast)
                 </span>
                </span>
               </li>
               <li>
                <span itemprop="ingredient" itemscope="" itemtype="http://data-vocabulary.org/RecipeIngredient">
                 <span itemprop="amount">
                  8 quarts
                 </span>
                 <span itemprop="name">
                  Cold Water
                 </span>
                </span>
               </li>
               <li>
                <span itemprop="ingredient" itemscope="" itemtype="http://data-vocabulary.org/RecipeIngredient">
                 <span itemprop="amount">
                 </span>
                 <span itemprop="name">
                  Half-and-half (healthy Splash Per Serving)
                 </span>
                </span>
               </li>
               <li>
                <span itemprop="ingredient" itemscope="" itemtype="http://data-vocabulary.org/RecipeIngredient">
                 <span itemprop="amount">
                 </span>
                 <span itemprop="name">
                  Sweetened Condensed Milk (2-3 Tablespoons Per Serving)
                 </span>
                </span>
               </li>
               <li>
                <span itemprop="ingredient" itemscope="" itemtype="http://data-vocabulary.org/RecipeIngredient">
                 <span itemprop="amount">
                 </span>
                 <span itemprop="name">
                  Note: Can Use Skim Milk, 2% Milk, Whole Milk, Sugar, Artificial Sweeteners, Syrups...adapt To Your Liking!
                 </span>
                </span>
               </li>
              </ul>
              <h4 class="recipe-sub-head">
               Preparation Instructions
              </h4>
              <div itemprop="instructions">
               <p>
                (Adapted from Imbibe Magazine)
               </p>
               <p>
                In a large container, mix ground coffee with water. Cover and allow to sit at room temperature eight hours or overnight.
               </p>
               <p>
                Line a fine mesh strainer with cheesecloth and set over a pitcher or other container. Pour coffee/water mixture through the strainer, allowing all liquid to run through. Discard grounds.
               </p>
               <p>
                Place coffee liquid in the fridge and allow to cool. Use as needed.
               </p>
               <p>
                To make iced coffee, pack a glass full of ice cubes. Fill glass 2/3 full with coffee liquid. Add healthy splash of half-and-half. Add 2-3 tablespoons sweetened condensed milk (can use plain sugar instead) and stir to combine. Taste and adjust half-and-half and/or sweetened condensed milk as needed.
               </p>
              </div>

               </h4>
               <p>
                Ditto.  Any leftover coffee gets frozen in ice cube trays and goes into a ziplock bag in the freezer.  Any time we want iced coffee, those are the cubes we use.
               </p>
              </div>
              <div class="clr">
              </div>
             </div>

              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/52ae11b769d14e284eb45607a20e0538?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
              <div class="comment-text">
               <h4>
                Yaya Cheryl
                <span>
                 On Tuesday, June 14 at 2:47 pm
                </span>
               </h4>
               <p>
                If you like frappuccinos, freeze some milk (I had some milk about to expire so I put a cup in a sandwich bag, froze flat on a cookie sheet, then put in a gallon freezer bag) thaw at 30% power for 30 seconds then put double strength coffee (add frozen cubes if you want it more frozen) in blender with milk.  I like mocha so I add chocolate syrup and a couple pkgs of stevia.  I know this is going to save me a lot of money since I now make frapps at home.
               </p>
              </div>

             <div class="comment even depth-2" id="comment-2842660">
              <p class="comment-number">
              </p>
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/17560a94596ab4b4aca1e63344e6da3d?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
              <div class="comment-text">
               <h4>
                She_Wolf
                <span>
                 On Sunday, July 17 at 9:22 pm
                </span>
               </h4>
               <p>
                If you have never heard of white coffee (sometimes called green coffee) then you probably have never been to Washington, Idaho or possibly northern Oregon and checked out one of their millions of coffee stands. Its WONDERFUL. It doesnt have the bitter taste of black coffee but has twice the caff. Its made in shots for espresso. (can be done with a french press at home) I have made iced coffee by the pitcher using the sweet and condensed milk before and it is similar to a McDonalds iced coffee. Yum. In an effort to create a frape using white coffee I decided to make the ice cubes after making an every increasing batch when I was trying to get it to taste just right. My favorite syrups are salted caramel and Irish Cream. They are so smooth and way good. Anyway long ramble short, check out thomas hammer coffee online and look for white zombie coffee. Its worth the investment! Oh and Torani syrups have the best flavor in my opinion.
                <img alt=":-)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://thepioneerwoman.com/cooking/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif"/>
                Thats just my 2 cents though.
               </p>

I make a similar drink with Caffix (a roasted grain beverage) that has almost the same taste without the shakes and tossing and turning at night!  I just mix some faux coffee in some water, add stevia to taste, and some nonfat powdered milk in a tall glass and then fill with ice cubes.  Sometimes I use a package of sugar (14 calories) or half and half (if Im not watching my weight).  When I am, I just use the powdered milk for that creamy taste even though it isnt as rich  I keep some Caffix in my purse too for when I go to a restaurant.  I put some in my water glasssince it usually tastes terribleand add a pkg of sugar or stevia  If they said anything, I just tell them I cant drink caffeinated drinks or soda pop, but they never do
               </p>
              </div>
              <div class="clr">
              </div>
             </div>

             <div class="comment even depth-2" id="comment-2779754">
              <p class="comment-number">
              </p>
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/f846ee991620e8ac629b1f1fd41c2e24?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
              <div class="comment-text">
               <h4>
                Robin
                <span>
                 On Tuesday, June 14 at 11:40 am
                </span>
               </h4>
               <p>
                Another option to the Toddy, is to use a french press. Use 2/3 cup of strong flavored ground coffee and 3 cups of cold water. Put the press in just until liquid begins to show through the screen. Let sit on the counter for 12 to 24 hours.
               </p>
               <p>
                When ready, press the grounds down and (Like Ree) pour liquid through a fine mesh sieve lined with a coffee filter. The ground stay in the press and the coffee filter strains out the finer sediment.
               </p>
               <p>
                Refridgerate and use in a 50/50 mix with cold milk or cold water over a glass full of ice. Can also be used in a 50/50 mix with water and heated for a cup of hot coffee.
               </p>
               <p>
                My family devours this in the summer so I make two presses at a time, every other day. Its a much more manageable quantity.
               </p>
              </div>
              <div class="clr">
              </div>
             </div>

            <div class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-2779209">
             <p class="comment-number">
              6
             </p>
             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/67bbf6d57b3309073479c08f6ecc8556?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <h4>
               Maggie
               <span>
                On Monday, June 13 at 6:32 am
               </span>
              </h4>
              <p>
               Im a former barista, and I miss having access to cold brewed iced coffee in large quantities!
              </p>
              <p>
               A note about the taste  because youre not adding hot water the coffee doesnt develop the same bitter notes that hot coffee (or hot coffee allowed to cool to be served as iced coffee  blech!) can have. So it should have some natural sweetness and the flavors of the coffee can really shine through. Its so worth it to try this with some good, single-origin fancy-pants coffee if you can get your hands on it. This also means it wont take as much sugar/syrup to achieve the level of sweetness you like.
              </p>
              <p>
               I encourage everyone to make cold brew at home, itll change your life!
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="clr">
             </div>

               <h4>
                Lisa
                <span>
                 On Tuesday, June 14 at 11:28 am
                </span>
               </h4>
               <p>
                Maggie is absolutely right; the cold-brewed coffee tastes significantly different (better!) than the hot-brewed then cooled coffee does. For that reason I wouldnt freeze regular brewed coffee into ice cubes because it will give the cold-brewed coffee a different flavor. I am an only-drink-it-sweet hot coffee girl and I dont even need or want much sweetner with the cold-brewed. Sallys idea about making a simple syrup is great because its hard to get sugar to dissolve in cold liquid. I make a much smaller quantity of the cold brew concentrate in my french press which lasts me several days. You have to try this!! It is soooo good.
               </p>
              </div>

              12
             </p>
             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0a988ba4d584e4c077edd860477b9543?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <h4>
               Aaron
               <span>
                On Monday, June 13 at 6:42 am
               </span>
              </h4>
              <p>
               Ive been doing this for years as well. 2 cups of ground coffee to 9 cups of water. Ive also found that steeping much longer than 12 hours causes the bitterness of the beans were trying to avoid to leech out into the brew, so Id recommend no more than 12-13 hours. Also, no sense buying an expensive contraption like the Toddy Maker when 2 normal sized pitchers will do the trick. If you like your coffee black as I do, I use a half coffee, half water mixture. Nice to see other people discovering this awesome thing!
              </p>
             </div>

              <div class="comment-text">

                <a class="url" href="http://www.fromthefrontporch.com/WPBlog" rel="external nofollow">
                 Ann from Montana
                </a>
                <span>
                 On Saturday, July 30 at 5:39 pm
                </span>
               </h4>
               <p>
                I reduced the whole thing to ounces and make the same proportions:
               </p>
               <p>
                2 ounces ground coffee
                <br/>
                32 ounces water (4 cups)
               </p>
               <p>
                I have a Chemex pot and filters so I pour my mix through a filter into the Chemex and the resulting concentrate fills 1 large mason jar  perfect for me as I dont have the frig storage space for the amount that Ree makes.
               </p>
               <p>
                Many Thanks to Ree for the whole enlightenment of concentrate.  IT IS WONDERFUL!!!
               </p>
               <p>
                *** I make a cinnamon simple syrup and use that, the concentrate and half and half  major YUM!
               </p>

             <div class="comment-text">
              <h4>
               <a class="url" href="http://hamletgrove.blogspot.com" rel="external nofollow">
                Blind Horse
               </a>
               <span>
                On Monday, June 13 at 7:03 am
               </span>
              </h4>
              <p>
               Fascinating, but for those of us hardy souls who drink our iced coffee black, is this going to be too strong?
              </p>
              <p>
               I make all my coffee in a french press, for iced coffee I simply brew with half the hot water, then add ice until its full.  The ice melts, making the brew strength just right, I press out the grounds and pour over more ice.  Divine!
              </p>
             </div>

               </h4>
               <p>
                If you want to sweeten your concentrate once its been filtered, that might be fine. I do believe you would be decreasing its shelf like. I dont think it would last as long as 3 weeks anymore. So, if you plan on drinking it up quick.
               </p>
               <p>
                I do not find it hard to sweeten my cold coffee to my liking. Its already fast enough that youre not brewing it etc. Just dump the concentrate in and some water/milk and some sugar. I sometimes use flavored coffee mates to sweeten mine.
               </p>

A friend in college did this to make regular coffee as well.  She let it soak for a good 24 hours, though, so it was more like coffee syrup.  Just add hot water instead of cold to reach your desired strength, and youre good to go.

             <div class="comment odd alt depth-2" id="comment-2780209">
              <p class="comment-number">
              </p>
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/99040101fade01d9c0a4cbd8d7a58184?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
              <div class="comment-text">
               <h4>
                Margaret
                <span>
                 On Friday, June 17 at 10:10 am
                </span>
               </h4>
               <p>
                I worked at Starbucks for many years. They brew double strength coffee with a blend they specially came up with for iced coffee called Terrazza. You can also buy Gazebo Blend in the summer months which makes a great iced coffee.
                <br/>
                The measurements for hot brewed are 2 tablespoons of coffee for 6 oz. water. So iced coffee would take 4 tablespoons for 6 oz . water. Sounds like a lot, but its what gives the coffee the full, complex flavor. Simple syrup is used to sweeten.
                <br/>
                They use a measuring beaker to get the right amount of ice cubes, sweetener and half-and -half.
               </p>
              </div>
              <div class="clr">
              </div>
             </div>

              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/e4e15edc6ace16495ce31540f400ba7d?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>

                </a>

                 On Saturday, July 30 at 5:48 pm
                </span>
               </h4>
               <p>
                YES to simple syrup.  The chemistry of making the syrup is the magic.  I make cinnamon syrup (simple syrup of 1 cup water, 1 cup sugar, add 4 cinnamon sticks after the sugar is disolved in the water and frig overnight then remove sticks).  1/2 concentrate, 1/2 half and half and cinnamon syrup to taste.  Thats my brew :)!
               </p>

             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/425c53fcd7e95cbd175d9f9f81802c36?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <h4>
               Widget
               <span>
                On Monday, June 13 at 8:17 am
               </span>
              </h4>
              <p>
               Heres smaller scale proportions:
               <br/>
               1/3 cup coffee
               <br/>
               12 ounces of water
               <br/>
               Cover container and chill overnight in fridge.
               <br/>
               Strain thru a coffee filter into a different pitcher/container
               <br/>
               Dilute concentrate with water/milk/etc. to your taste.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="clr">

              <p>
               Ive been doing this for a few years now and it is truly wonderful-makes a great extract thats super concentrated, rich and smooth without bitterness. And it can really pack a punch. The ratio I use ( I think it came from a recipe in the NY Times) is 1 lb. course ground coffee to 10 cups water and I let it stand overnight at room temp. before filtering into a decanter for the fridge. Yummy and easy- just like Ree says.
              </p>

Also  you can use the ground twice.  I let my concentrate sit for 48 hours and it is super concentrated, only a few table spoons and some cold water!

              <p class="comment-number">
              </p>
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/81303c9cbb30b81cbaa4ee2cec39e4f0?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
              <div class="comment-text">
               <h4>
                Carla
                <span>
                 On Saturday, August 20 at 2:42 pm
                </span>
               </h4>
               <p>
                Didnt notice this in the comments; but didnt read them all.  Yet.
                <img alt=":P" class="wp-smiley" src="http://thepioneerwoman.com/cooking/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_razz.gif"/>
               </p>
               <p>
                What she didnt mention is that cold brewing coffee like this (or similar) takes all the acidity out of it.  No bitterness!  No upset stomach for those who have trouble with coffee.  Even cheap coffee comes out fairly decent when brewed this way.
               </p>
               <p>
                Once you get used to it, coffee brewed the normal way tastes like cigarette ashes.  It really does spoil a person!
               </p>
               <p>
                They do make cold brew pots  I like the hourglass one.  It makes enough coffee extract for me to have 2-3 cups of coffee (hot or iced) for a week and a half or two weeks.  I take a jar to work and I keep some at home.  Its really great!  I take it on the road when I travel.
               </p>
               <p>
                And I just opened a can of scm; ill have to try the vietnamese idea.
               </p>

                I think you can get one from Pottery Barn, too. Item No. 30-8978348.
               </p>
              </div>

             <p class="comment-number">
              98
             </p>
             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-54 photo" height="54" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/ec94fadad580c444e332c09005479a0d?s=54&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fthepioneerwoman.com%2Fcooking%2Fwp-content%2Fthemes%2Fmulti%2Fimages%2Fcomment-avatar-3.gif%3F1%26s%3D54&amp;r=G" width="54"/>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <h4>
               <a class="url" href="http://www.eatplayread.wordpress.com" rel="external nofollow">
                Emily @ EatPlayRead
               </a>
               <span>
                On Monday, June 13 at 8:43 am
               </span>
              </h4>
              <p>
               I stumbled across the cold brew method as well, and I love it! It makes delicious iced coffee. I dont make such a huge amount though. I make about 4 cups of it in my french press at a time, and store it in the fridge. It definitely makes the best iced coffee ever!
              </p>
             </div>

            My Cookbooks
           </a>
          </h3>
          <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Ree-Drummond/e/B002GWKP96/ref=dp_byline_cont_book_1">
           <img src="http://thepioneerwoman.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/cookbooks.jpg"/>
          </a>
          <div class="post-info">
           <p>
            I love writing cookbooks, and I pour my heart and soul into each and every one! They're full of my very favorite recipes, photos of life on the ranch, and lots and lots of love.
           </p>
